## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The equation of motion for such systems typically involves restoring forces (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Cubic nonlinear restoring force (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator without damping)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing oscillator with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (Duffing with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v (nonlinear friction dependent on position)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven softening oscillator)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force for pendulum)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 (coupled position-velocity nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) â†’ symmetric potential wells characteristic of Duffing-type oscillators
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x**2)*v â†’ self-excited oscillations (Van der Pol type limit cycles)
- Negative linear damping with positive cubic velocity damping â†’ amplitude-limiting self-oscillation
- Sinusoidal time dependence in acceleration â†’ externally driven/forced oscillator
- Sign of cubic coefficient relative to linear term â†’ hardening spring (same sign as linear) vs softening spring (opposite sign)
- Position-velocity product terms x^n * v^m â†’ energy-dependent damping or nonlinear dissipation
- Sinusoidal function of position sin(c*x) â†’ large-amplitude pendulum or periodic potential dynamics
- Absence of explicit time dependence â†’ autonomous/conservative system; presence â†’ driven or time-varying system
